      <tr>
       <td style="padding:0.3em 0.4em 0.3em;font-weight:bold;border-top: 1px solid #aaa; border-bottom: 1px solid #aaa;">
        <div class="hlist" style="text-align:center;font-size:90%;font-weight:normal;">
         <ul>
          <li>
           <a href="/wiki/Outline_of_political_science#Politics_by_region" title="Outline of political science">
            Other countries
           </a>
          </li>
          <li>
           <a class="extiw" href="//commons.wikimedia.org/wiki/Atlas_of_Vatican_City" title="commons:Atlas of Vatican City">
            Atlas
           </a>
          </li>
         </ul>
         <p>
          <span class="metadata">
           <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:A_coloured_voting_box.svg">
            <img alt="Portal icon" class="thumbborder" data-file-height="160" data-file-width="160" height="16" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/0/01/A_coloured_voting_box.svg/16px-A_coloured_voting_box.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/0/01/A_coloured_voting_box.svg/24px-A_coloured_voting_box.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/0/01/A_coloured_voting_box.svg/32px-A_coloured_voting_box.svg.png 2x" width="16"/>
           </a>
          </span>
          <a href="/wiki/Portal:Politics" title="Portal:Politics">
           Politics portal
          </a>
         </p>
        </div>
       </td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
       <td style="text-align:right;font-size:115%;padding-top: 0.6em;">
        <div class="plainlinks hlist navbar mini">
         <ul>
          <li class="nv-view">
           <a href="/wiki/Template:Politics_of_Vatican_City" title="Template:Politics of Vatican City">
            <span title="View this template">
             v
            </span>
           </a>
          </li>
          <li class="nv-talk">
           <a href="/wiki/Template_talk:Politics_of_Vatican_City" title="Template talk:Politics of Vatican City">
            <span title="Discuss this template">
             t
            </span>
           </a>
          </li>
          <li class="nv-edit">
           <a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Template:Politics_of_Vatican_City&amp;action=edit">
            <span title="Edit this template">
             e
            </span>
           </a>
          </li>
         </ul>
        </div>
       </td>
      </tr>
     </table>
     <div class="hatnote relarticle mainarticle">
      Main article:
      <a href="/wiki/Politics_of_Vatican_City" title="Politics of Vatican City">
       Politics of Vatican City
      </a>
     </div>
     <p>
      The politics of Vatican City takes place in an
      <a href="/wiki/Absolute_monarchy" title="Absolute monarchy">
       absolute
      </a>
      <a href="/wiki/Elective_monarchy" title="Elective monarchy">
       elective monarchy
      </a>
      , in which the head of the Roman Catholic Church takes power. The Pope exercises principal legislative, executive, and judicial power over the State of Vatican City (an entity distinct from the
      <a href="/wiki/Holy_See" title="Holy See">
       Holy See
      </a>
      ), which is a rare case of a non-hereditary monarchy.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-nationsencyclopedia1_54-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-nationsencyclopedia1-54">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        49
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      Vatican City is currently the only widely recognized independent state that has not become a member of the United Nations. The Holy See, which is distinct from Vatican City State, has
      <a href="/wiki/United_Nations_General_Assembly_observers" title="United Nations General Assembly observers">
       permanent observer status
      </a>
      with all the rights of a full member except for a vote in the
      <a href="/wiki/United_Nations_General_Assembly" title="United Nations General Assembly">
       UN General Assembly
      </a>
      .
     </p>
     <h3>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="Political_system">
       Political system
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=Vatican_City&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: Political system">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h3>
     <p>
      The government of Vatican City has a unique structure. The Pope is the sovereign of the state. Legislative authority is vested in the
      <a href="/wiki/Pontifical_Commission_for_Vatican_City_State" title="Pontifical Commission for Vatican City State">
       Pontifical Commission for Vatican City State
      </a>
      , a body of cardinals appointed by the Pope for five-year periods. Executive power is in the hands of the President of that commission, assisted by the General Secretary and Deputy General Secretary. The state's foreign relations are entrusted to the Holy See's
      <a href="/wiki/Secretariat_of_State_(Holy_See)" title="Secretariat of State (Holy See)">
       Secretariat of State
      </a>
      and diplomatic service. Nevertheless, the pope has both absolute power in the executive, legislative and judicial branches over Vatican City. He is currently the only absolute monarch in Europe.
     </p>
     <p>
      There are specific departments that deal with health, security, telecommunications, etc.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-55">
       <a href="#cite_note-55">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        50
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      The
      <a href="/wiki/Camerlengo_of_the_Holy_Roman_Church" title="Camerlengo of the Holy Roman Church">
       Cardinal Camerlengo
      </a>
      presides over the
      <a href="/wiki/Apostolic_Camera" title="Apostolic Camera">
       Apostolic Camera
      </a>
      to which is entrusted the administration of the property and the protection of the temporal rights of the Holy See during a
      <a href="/wiki/Sede_vacante" title="Sede vacante">
       papal vacancy
      </a>
      . Those of the Vatican State remain under the control of the Pontifical Commission for the State of Vatican City. Acting with three other cardinals chosen by lot every three days, one from each order of cardinals (cardinal bishop, cardinal priest, and cardinal deacon), he in a sense performs during that period the functions of head of state of Vatican City.
      <sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">
       [
       <i>
        <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed">
         <span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (February 2013)">
          citation needed
         </span>
        </a>
       </i>
       ]
      </sup>
      All the decisions these four cardinals take must be approved by the
      <a href="/wiki/College_of_Cardinals" title="College of Cardinals">
       College of Cardinals
      </a>
      as a whole.
     </p>
     <p>
      The nobility that was closely associated with the Holy See at the time of the Papal States continued to be associated with the Papal Court after the loss of these territories, generally with merely nominal duties (see
      <a href="/wiki/Master_of_the_Horse#Papal_Master_of_the_Horse" title="Master of the Horse">
       Papal Master of the Horse
      </a>
      ,
      <a href="/wiki/Prefecture_of_the_Pontifical_Household" title="Prefecture of the Pontifical Household">
       Prefecture of the Pontifical Household
      </a>
      ,
      <a href="/wiki/Hereditary_officers_of_the_Roman_Curia" title="Hereditary officers of the Roman Curia">
       Hereditary officers of the Roman Curia
      </a>
      ,
      <a href="/wiki/Black_Nobility" title="Black Nobility">
       Black Nobility
      </a>
      ). They also formed the ceremonial Noble Guard. In the first decades of the existence of the Vatican City State,
      <a href="/wiki/Executive_(government)" title="Executive (government)">
       executive functions
      </a>
      were entrusted to some of them, including that of Delegate for the State of Vatican City (now denominated President of the Commission for Vatican City). But with the
      <a href="/wiki/Motu_proprio" title="Motu proprio">
       motu proprio
      </a>
      <i>
       <a href="/wiki/Pontificalis_Domus" title="Pontificalis Domus">
        Pontificalis Domus
       </a>
      </i>
      of 28 March 1968,
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-56">
       <a href="#cite_note-56">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        51
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <a href="/wiki/Pope_Paul_VI" title="Pope Paul VI">
       Pope Paul VI
      </a>
      abolished the honorary positions that had continued to exist until then, such as
      <a href="/wiki/Quartermaster_general" title="Quartermaster general">
       Quartermaster general
      </a>
      and
      <a href="/wiki/Master_of_the_Horse" title="Master of the Horse">
       Master of the Horse
      </a>
      .
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-57">
       <a href="#cite_note-57">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        52
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      Vatican City State, created in 1929 by the Lateran Pacts, provides the Holy See with a temporal jurisdiction and independence within a small territory. It is distinct from the Holy See. The state can thus be deemed a significant but not essential instrument of the Holy See. The Holy See itself has existed continuously as a juridical entity since Roman Imperial times and has been internationally recognized as a powerful and independent sovereign entity since
      <a href="/wiki/Late_Antiquity" title="Late Antiquity">
       Late Antiquity
      </a>
      to the present, without interruption even at times when it was deprived of territory (e.g. 1870 to 1929). The Holy See has the oldest active continuous diplomatic service in the world, dating back to at least AD 325 with its legation to the
      <a href="/wiki/First_Council_of_Nicaea" title="First Council of Nicaea">
       Council of Nicea
      </a>
      .
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-58">
       <a href="#cite_note-58">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        53
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <h3>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="Head_of_state">
       Head of state
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=Vatican_City&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: Head of state">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h3>
     <div class="hatnote relarticle mainarticle">
      Main article:
      <a href="/wiki/Pope" title="Pope">
       Pope
      </a>
     </div>
     <div class="hatnote">
      See also:
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/List_of_Sovereigns_of_the_Vatican_City_State" title="List of Sovereigns of the Vatican City State">
       List of Sovereigns of the Vatican City State
      </a>
     </div>
     <div class="thumb tright">
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
       <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:025Angelus.JPG">
        <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="600" data-file-width="800" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/47/025Angelus.JPG/220px-025Angelus.JPG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/47/025Angelus.JPG/330px-025Angelus.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/47/025Angelus.JPG/440px-025Angelus.JPG 2x" width="220"/>
       </a>
       <div class="thumbcaption">
        <div class="magnify">
         <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:025Angelus.JPG" title="Enlarge">
         </a>
        </div>
        The
        <a href="/wiki/Apostolic_Palace" title="Apostolic Palace">
         Apostolic Palace
        </a>
        (
        <i>
         Palazzo Apostolico
        </i>
        ), the official residence of the Pope. Here, Benedict XVI is at the window marked by a maroon banner hanging from the windowsill at centre.
       </div>
      </div>
     </div>
     <p>
      The Pope is
      <a href="/wiki/Ex_officio_member" title="Ex officio member">
       <i>
        ex officio
       </i>
      </a>
      <a href="/wiki/Head_of_state" title="Head of state">
       head of state
      </a>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-59">
       <a href="#cite_note-59">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        54
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      of Vatican City, functions dependent on his primordial function as bishop of the
      <a href="/wiki/Diocese_of_Rome" title="Diocese of Rome">
       diocese of Rome
      </a>
      . The term
      <a href="/wiki/Holy_See" title="Holy See">
       Holy See
      </a>
      refers not to the Vatican state but to the Pope's spiritual and pastoral governance, largely exercised through the
      <a href="/wiki/Roman_Curia" title="Roman Curia">
       Roman Curia
      </a>
      .
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-60">
       <a href="#cite_note-60">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        55
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      His official title with regard to Vatican City is
      <i>
       Sovereign of the State of the Vatican City
      </i>
      .
     </p>
     <p>
      <a href="/wiki/Pope_Francis" title="Pope Francis">
       Pope Francis
      </a>
      , born Jorge Mario Bergoglio in
      <a href="/wiki/Buenos_Aires" title="Buenos Aires">
       Buenos Aires
      </a>
      ,
      <a href="/wiki/Argentina" title="Argentina">
       Argentina
      </a>
      , was
      <a href="/wiki/Papal_conclave,_2013" title="Papal conclave, 2013">
       elected
      </a>
      on 13 March 2013. Francis took the unusual decision to live in the Vatican's guest house,
      <a href="/wiki/Domus_Sanctae_Marthae" title="Domus Sanctae Marthae">
       Domus Sanctae Marthae
      </a>
      , rather than the
      <a href="/wiki/Papal_Apartments" title="Papal Apartments">
       Papal Apartments
      </a>
      of the
      <a href="/wiki/Apostolic_Palace" title="Apostolic Palace">
       Apostolic Palace
      </a>
      which is the official papal residence. He still carries out his business and meets foreign representatives in the Palace.
     </p>
     <p>
      His principal subordinate government official for Vatican City is the
      <a href="/wiki/President_of_the_Pontifical_Commission_for_Vatican_City_State" title="President of the Pontifical Commission for Vatican City State">
       President of the Pontifical Commission for Vatican City State
      </a>
      , who since 1952 exercises the functions previously belonging to the
      <a href="/wiki/Governor_of_Vatican_City" title="Governor of Vatican City">
       Governor of Vatican City
      </a>
      . Since 2001, the President of the Pontifical Commission for Vatican City State also has the title of President of the Governorate of the State of Vatican City. The current President is Italian Cardinal
      <a href="/wiki/Giuseppe_Bertello" title="Giuseppe Bertello">
       Giuseppe Bertello
      </a>
      , who was appointed on 1 October 2011.
     </p>
     <h3>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="Administration">
       Administration
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=Vatican_City&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: Administration">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h3>
     <p>
      <a href="/wiki/Legislature" title="Legislature">
       Legislative
      </a>
      functions are delegated to the
      <a href="/wiki/Unicameralism" title="Unicameralism">
       unicameral
      </a>
      <a href="/wiki/Pontifical_Commission_for_Vatican_City_State" title="Pontifical Commission for Vatican City State">
       Pontifical Commission for Vatican City State
      </a>
      , led by the
      <a href="/wiki/President_of_the_Pontifical_Commission_for_Vatican_City_State" title="President of the Pontifical Commission for Vatican City State">
       President of the Pontifical Commission for Vatican City State
      </a>
      . Its seven members are cardinals appointed by the pope for terms of five years. Acts of the commission must be approved by the pope, through the Holy See's
      <a href="/wiki/Secretariat_of_State_(Holy_See)" title="Secretariat of State (Holy See)">
       Secretariat of State
      </a>
      , and before taking effect must be published in a special appendix of the
      <i>
       <a href="/wiki/Acta_Apostolicae_Sedis" title="Acta Apostolicae Sedis">
        Acta Apostolicae Sedis
       </a>
      </i>
      . Most of the content of this appendix consists of routine executive decrees, such as approval for a new set of postage stamps.
     </p>
     <p>
      <a href="/wiki/Executive_(government)" title="Executive (government)">
       Executive authority
      </a>
      is delegated to the Governorate of Vatican City. The Governorate consists of the President of the Pontifical Commissionusing the title "President of the Governorate of Vatican City"a general secretary, and a Vice general secretary, each appointed by the pope for five-year terms. Important actions of the Governorate must be confirmed by the Pontifical Commission and by the Pope through the Secretariat of State.
     </p>
     <p>
      The Governorate oversees the central governmental functions through several departments and offices. The directors and officials of these offices are appointed by the pope for five-year terms. These organs concentrate on material questions concerning the state's territory, including local security, records, transportation, and finances. The Governorate oversees a modern security &amp; police corps, the
      <i>
       <a href="/wiki/Corps_of_Gendarmerie_of_Vatican_City" title="Corps of Gendarmerie of Vatican City">
        Corpo della Gendarmeria dello Stato della Citt del Vaticano
       </a>
      </i>
      .
     </p>
     <p>
      <a href="/wiki/Judiciary" title="Judiciary">
       Judicial
      </a>
      functions are delegated to a supreme court, an appellate court, a tribunal (
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Tribunal_of_Vatican_City_State" title="Tribunal of Vatican City State">
       Tribunal of Vatican City State
      </a>
      ), and a trial judge. At the Vatican's request, sentences imposed can be served in Italy (see the
      <a href="#Crime">
       section on crime
      </a>
      , below).
     </p>
     <p>
      The
      <a href="/wiki/Postal_code#Country_code_prefixes" title="Postal code">
       international postal country code prefix
      </a>
      is
      <i>
       SCV
      </i>
      , and the only postal code is
      <i>
       00120
      </i>
       altogether
      <i>
       SCV-00120
      </i>
      .
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-61">
       <a href="#cite_note-61">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        56
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <h3>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="Defence_and_security">
       Defence and security
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=Vatican_City&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: Defence and security">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h3>
     <div class="thumb tright">
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
       <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Pontifical_Swiss_Guards_in_their_traditional_uniform.jpg">
        <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="460" data-file-width="320" height="316" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/93/Pontifical_Swiss_Guards_in_their_traditional_uniform.jpg/220px-Pontifical_Swiss_Guards_in_their_traditional_uniform.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/9/93/Pontifical_Swiss_Guards_in_their_traditional_uniform.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/9/93/Pontifical_Swiss_Guards_in_their_traditional_uniform.jpg 2x" width="220"/>
       </a>
       <div class="thumbcaption">
        <div class="magnify">
         <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Pontifical_Swiss_Guards_in_their_traditional_uniform.jpg" title="Enlarge">
         </a>
        </div>
        <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Pontifical_Swiss_Guard" title="Pontifical Swiss Guard">
         Pontifical Swiss Guards
        </a>
        in their traditional uniform
       </div>
      </div>
     </div>
     <div class="thumb tleft">
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
       <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Fiat_Bravo_Gendarmeria_Vaticana.png">
        <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="457" data-file-width="801" height="126" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6a/Fiat_Bravo_Gendarmeria_Vaticana.png/220px-Fiat_Bravo_Gendarmeria_Vaticana.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6a/Fiat_Bravo_Gendarmeria_Vaticana.png/330px-Fiat_Bravo_Gendarmeria_Vaticana.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6a/Fiat_Bravo_Gendarmeria_Vaticana.png/440px-Fiat_Bravo_Gendarmeria_Vaticana.png 2x" width="220"/>
       </a>
       <div class="thumbcaption">
        <div class="magnify">
         <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Fiat_Bravo_Gendarmeria_Vaticana.png" title="Enlarge">
         </a>
        </div>
        <a href="/wiki/Corps_of_Gendarmerie_of_Vatican_City" title="Corps of Gendarmerie of Vatican City">
         Gendarmerie
        </a>
        Police car
       </div>
      </div>
     </div>
     <div class="hatnote relarticle mainarticle">
      Main articles:
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Military_of_Vatican_City" title="Military of Vatican City">
       Military of Vatican City
      </a>
      ,
      <a href="/wiki/Corps_of_Gendarmerie_of_Vatican_City" title="Corps of Gendarmerie of Vatican City">
       Corps of Gendarmerie of Vatican City
      </a>
      and
      <a href="/wiki/Corps_of_Firefighters_of_the_Vatican_City_State" title="Corps of Firefighters of the Vatican City State">
       Corps of Firefighters of the Vatican City State
      </a>
     </div>
     <p>
      As the Vatican City is an enclave within Italy, its military defence is provided by the Italian
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Military_of_Italy" title="Military of Italy">
       armed forces
      </a>
      . Vatican City has no armed forces of its own, although the
      <a href="/wiki/Swiss_Guard" title="Swiss Guard">
       Swiss Guard
      </a>
      is a military corps of the Holy See responsible for the personal security of the Pope, and resident in the state. Soldiers of the Swiss Guard are entitled to hold Vatican City State passports and nationality. Swiss
      <a href="/wiki/Mercenary" title="Mercenary">
       mercenaries
      </a>
      were historically recruited by Popes as part of an army for the Papal States, and the
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Pontifical_Swiss_Guard" title="Pontifical Swiss Guard">
       Pontifical Swiss Guard
      </a>
      was founded by
      <a href="/wiki/Pope_Julius_II" title="Pope Julius II">
       Pope Julius II
      </a>
      on 22 January 1506 as the pope's personal bodyguard and continues to fulfill that function. It is listed in the
      <a href="/wiki/Annuario_Pontificio" title="Annuario Pontificio">
       Annuario Pontificio
      </a>
      under "Holy See", not under "State of Vatican City". At the end of 2005, the Guard had 134 members. Recruitment is arranged by a special agreement between the Holy See and
      <a href="/wiki/Switzerland" title="Switzerland">
       Switzerland
      </a>
      . All recruits must be Catholic, unmarried males with Swiss citizenship who have completed their
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Basic_training" title="Basic training">
       basic training
      </a>
      with the
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Swiss_Army" title="Swiss Army">
       Swiss Army
      </a>
      with certificates of good conduct, be between the ages of 19 and 30, and be at least 174cm (5ft 9in) in height. Members are equipped with
      <a href="/wiki/Small_arms" title="Small arms">
       small arms
      </a>
      and the traditional
      <a href="/wiki/Halberd" title="Halberd">
       halberd
      </a>
      (also called the Swiss voulge), and trained in bodyguarding tactics. The
      <a href="/wiki/Palatine_Guard" title="Palatine Guard">
       Palatine Guard
      </a>
      and the
      <a href="/wiki/Noble_Guard_(Vatican)" title="Noble Guard (Vatican)">
       Noble Guard
      </a>
      , the last armed forces of the Vatican City State, were disbanded by
      <a href="/wiki/Pope_Paul_VI" title="Pope Paul VI">
       Pope Paul VI
      </a>
      in 1970.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Vatican_State_36-1">
       <a href="#cite_note-Vatican_State-36">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        31
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      Civil defence is the responsibility of the
      <a href="/wiki/Corps_of_Firefighters_of_the_Vatican_City_State" title="Corps of Firefighters of the Vatican City State">
       Corps of Firefighters of the Vatican City State
      </a>
      , the national
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Fire_brigade" title="Fire brigade">
       fire brigade
      </a>
      . Dating its origins to the early nineteenth century, the Corps in its present form was established in 1941. It is responsible for fire fighting, as well as a range of civil defence scenarios including flood, natural disaster, and mass casualty management. The Corps is governmentally supervised through the Directorate for Security Services and Civil Defence, which is also responsible for the Gendarmerie (see below).
     </p>
     <p>
      The
      <a href="/wiki/Corps_of_Gendarmerie_of_Vatican_City" title="Corps of Gendarmerie of Vatican City">
       Gendarmerie Corps
      </a>
      (
      <i>
       Corpo della Gendarmeria
      </i>
      ) is the
      <a href="/wiki/Gendarmerie" title="Gendarmerie">
       gendarmerie
      </a>
      , or police and security force, of Vatican City and the
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Extraterritorial_properties_of_the_Holy_See" title="Extraterritorial properties of the Holy See">
       extraterritorial properties of the Holy See
      </a>
      .
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-62">
       <a href="#cite_note-62">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        57
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      The corps is responsible for security,
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Public_order" title="Public order">
       public order
      </a>
      ,
      <a href="/wiki/Border_control" title="Border control">
       border control
      </a>
      ,
      <a href="/wiki/Road_traffic_control" title="Road traffic control">
       traffic control
      </a>
      ,
      <a href="/wiki/Criminal_procedure" title="Criminal procedure">
       criminal investigation
      </a>
      , and other general police duties in Vatican City including providing security for the pope outside of Vatican City. The corps has 130 personnel and is a part of the Directorate for Security Services and Civil Defence (which also includes the Vatican Fire Brigade), an organ of the Governorate of Vatican City.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Gendarme_63-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-Gendarme-63">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        58
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Administrations_64-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-Administrations-64">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        59
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <h3>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="Foreign_relations">
       Foreign relations
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=Vatican_City&amp;action=edit&amp;section=17" title="Edit section: Foreign relations">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h3>
     <div class="thumb tright">
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
       <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:0_Palazzo_del_Governatorato_-_Vatican.JPG">
        <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2592" data-file-width="3888" height="147" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c1/0_Palazzo_del_Governatorato_-_Vatican.JPG/220px-0_Palazzo_del_Governatorato_-_Vatican.JPG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c1/0_Palazzo_del_Governatorato_-_Vatican.JPG/330px-0_Palazzo_del_Governatorato_-_Vatican.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c1/0_Palazzo_del_Governatorato_-_Vatican.JPG/440px-0_Palazzo_del_Governatorato_-_Vatican.JPG 2x" width="220"/>
       </a>
       <div class="thumbcaption">
        <div class="magnify">
         <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:0_Palazzo_del_Governatorato_-_Vatican.JPG" title="Enlarge">
         </a>
        </div>
        Palace of the Governorate of Vatican City State
       </div>
      </div>
     </div>
     <div class="thumb tright">
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
       <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Vatican_City_-_main_entrance_with_Swiss_Guard.jpg">
        <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="3072" data-file-width="2304" height="293" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/08/Vatican_City_-_main_entrance_with_Swiss_Guard.jpg/220px-Vatican_City_-_main_entrance_with_Swiss_Guard.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/08/Vatican_City_-_main_entrance_with_Swiss_Guard.jpg/330px-Vatican_City_-_main_entrance_with_Swiss_Guard.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/08/Vatican_City_-_main_entrance_with_Swiss_Guard.jpg/440px-Vatican_City_-_main_entrance_with_Swiss_Guard.jpg 2x" width="220"/>
       </a>
       <div class="thumbcaption">
        <div class="magnify">
         <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Vatican_City_-_main_entrance_with_Swiss_Guard.jpg" title="Enlarge">
         </a>
        </div>
        An entrance to Vatican City from Italy
       </div>
      </div>
     </div>
     <div class="hatnote">
      See also:
      <a href="/wiki/Foreign_relations_of_the_Holy_See" title="Foreign relations of the Holy See">
       Foreign relations of the Holy See
      </a>
      and
      <a href="/wiki/List_of_diplomatic_missions_of_the_Holy_See" title="List of diplomatic missions of the Holy See">
       List of diplomatic missions of the Holy See
      </a>
     </div>
     <p>
      Vatican City State is a recognized national territory under international law, but it is the Holy See that conducts diplomatic relations on its behalf, in addition to the Holy See's own diplomacy, entering into
      <a href="/wiki/Treaty" title="Treaty">
       international agreements
      </a>
      in its regard. Vatican City thus has no diplomatic service of its own.
     </p>
     <p>
      Because of space limitations, Vatican City is one of the few countries in the world that is unable to host embassies. Foreign embassies to the Holy See are located in the city of Rome; only during the Second World War were the staff of some embassies accredited to the Holy See given what hospitality was possible within the narrow confines of Vatican Cityembassies such as that of the United Kingdom while Rome was held by the Axis Powers and Germany's when the Allies controlled Rome.
     </p>
     <p>
      The size of Vatican City is thus unrelated to the large global reach exercised by the Holy See as an entity quite distinct from the state.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-65">
       <a href="#cite_note-65">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        60
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      However, Vatican City State itself participates in some international organizations whose functions relate to the state as a geographical entity, distinct from the non-territorial legal persona of the Holy See. These organizations are much less numerous than those in which the Holy See participates either as a member or with observer status. They include the following eight, in each of which Vatican City State holds membership:
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Participation_66-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-Participation-66">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        61
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-67">
       <a href="#cite_note-67">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        62
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <ul>
      <li>
       <a href="/wiki/European_Conference_of_Postal_and_Telecommunications_Administrations" title="European Conference of Postal and Telecommunications Administrations">
        European Conference of Postal and Telecommunications Administrations
       </a>
       (CEPT)
      </li>
      <li>
       <a href="/wiki/Eutelsat" title="Eutelsat">
        European Telecommunications Satellite Organization
       </a>
       (Eutelsat IGO)
      </li>
      <li>
       <a href="/wiki/International_Grains_Agreement" title="International Grains Agreement">
        International Grains Council
       </a>
       (IGC)
      </li>
      <li>
       <a href="/wiki/International_Institute_of_Administrative_Sciences" title="International Institute of Administrative Sciences">
        International Institute of Administrative Sciences
       </a>
       (IIAS)
      </li>
      <li>
       <a href="/wiki/International_Telecommunication_Union" title="International Telecommunication Union">
        International Telecommunication Union
       </a>
       (ITU)
      </li>
      <li>
       <a href="/wiki/International_Telecommunications_Satellite_Organization" title="International Telecommunications Satellite Organization">
        International Telecommunications Satellite Organization
       </a>
       (ITSO)
      </li>
      <li>
       <a href="/wiki/Interpol" title="Interpol">
        Interpol
       </a>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-68">
        <a href="#cite_note-68">
         <span>
          [
         </span>
         63
         <span>
          ]
         </span>
        </a>
       </sup>
      </li>
      <li>
       <a href="/wiki/Universal_Postal_Union" title="Universal Postal Union">
        Universal Postal Union
       </a>
       (UPU)
      </li>
     </ul>
     <p>
      It also participates in:
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Participation_66-1">
       <a href="#cite_note-Participation-66">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        61
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <ul>
      <li>
       <a href="/wiki/World_Medical_Association" title="World Medical Association">
        World Medical Association
       </a>
      </li>
      <li>
       <a href="/wiki/World_Intellectual_Property_Organization" title="World Intellectual Property Organization">
        World Intellectual Property Organization
       </a>
       (WIPO)
      </li>
     </ul>
     <h2>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="Economy">
       Economy
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=Vatican_City&amp;action=edit&amp;section=18" title="Edit section: Economy">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h2>
     <div class="hatnote relarticle mainarticle">
      Main article:
      <a href="/wiki/Economy_of_Vatican_City" title="Economy of Vatican City">
       Economy of Vatican City
      </a>
     </div>
     <p>
      The Vatican City State budget includes the
      <a href="/wiki/Vatican_Museums" title="Vatican Museums">
       Vatican Museums
      </a>
      and post office and is supported financially by the sale of
      <a href="/wiki/Postage_stamps_and_postal_history_of_Vatican_City" title="Postage stamps and postal history of Vatican City">
       stamps
      </a>
      ,
      <a href="/wiki/Vatican_euro_coins" title="Vatican euro coins">
       coins
      </a>
      , medals and tourist mementos; by fees for admission to museums; and by publications sales.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-69">
       <a href="#cite_note-69">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        f
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      The incomes and living standards of lay workers are comparable to those of counterparts who work in the city of Rome.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-economy_factbook_70-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-economy_factbook-70">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        64
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      Other industries include printing, the production of mosaics, and the manufacture of staff uniforms.
     </p>
     <p>
      The
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Institute_for_Works_of_Religion" title="Institute for Works of Religion">
       Institute for Works of Religion
      </a>
      , also known as the Vatican Bank, and with the acronym IOR (
      <i>
       Istituto per le Opere di Religione
      </i>
      ), is a bank situated in the Vatican that conducts worldwide financial activities. It has an
      <a href="/wiki/Automated_teller_machine" title="Automated teller machine">
       ATM
      </a>
      with instructions in
      <a href="/wiki/Latin" title="Latin">
       Latin
      </a>
      , possibly the only such ATM in the world.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-71">
       <a href="#cite_note-71">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        65
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      Vatican City issues its own coins. It has used the euro as its currency since 1 January 1999, owing to a special agreement with the European Union (council decision 1999/98). Euro coins and notes were introduced on 1 January 2002the Vatican does not issue
      <a href="/wiki/Euro_banknotes" title="Euro banknotes">
       euro banknotes
      </a>
      . Issuance of euro-denominated coins is strictly limited by treaty, though somewhat more than usual is allowed in a year in which there is a change in the papacy.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-72">
       <a href="#cite_note-72">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        66
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      Because of their rarity, Vatican euro coins are highly sought by collectors.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-73">
       <a href="#cite_note-73">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        67
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      Until the adoption of the Euro, Vatican coinage and stamps were denominated in their own
      <a href="/wiki/Vatican_lira" title="Vatican lira">
       Vatican lira
      </a>
      currency, which was on par with the Italian
      <a href="/wiki/Lira" title="Lira">
       lira
      </a>
      .
     </p>
     <p>
      Vatican City State, which employs nearly 2,000 people, had a surplus of 6.7million euros in 2007 but ran a deficit in 2008 of over 15million euros.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-74">
       <a href="#cite_note-74">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        68
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      In 2012, the U.S. State Department's International Narcotics Control Strategy Report listed Vatican City for the first time among the nations of concern for money-laundering, placing it in the middle category, which includes countries such as Ireland, but not among the most vulnerable countries, which include the United States itself, Germany, Italy and Russia.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-75">
       <a href="#cite_note-75">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        69
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      On 24 February 2014 the Vatican announced it was establishing a secretariat for the economy which will be responsible for all economic, financial and administrative activities of the Holy See and the Vatican City State. Cardinal
      <a href="/wiki/George_Pell" title="George Pell">
       George Pell
      </a>
      is to head up the secretariat, the formation of which follows the charging last month of two senior clerics including a monsignor with money laundering.
      <a href="/wiki/Pope_Francis" title="Pope Francis">
       Pope Francis
      </a>
      also appointed an auditor-general authorized to do random audits of any agency at any time, and engaged a US financial services company to review the Vatican's 19,000 accounts to ensure compliance with international money laundering practices. The pontiff also ordered that the
      <a href="/wiki/Administration_of_the_Patrimony_of_the_Apostolic_See" title="Administration of the Patrimony of the Apostolic See">
       Administration of the Patrimony of the Apostolic See
      </a>
      will become the Vatican's central bank, with responsibilities similar to other central banks around the world.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-VaticanEconomicSecretariat_76-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-VaticanEconomicSecretariat-76">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        70
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <h2>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="Demographics">
       Demographics
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">

        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h2>
     <h3>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="Population_and_languages">
       Population and languages
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=Vatican_City&amp;action=edit&amp;section=20" title="Edit section: Population and languages">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h3>

      <a href="/wiki/Languages_of_Vatican_City" title="Languages of Vatican City">

       <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Seal_of_Vatican_City.svg">
        <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="755" data-file-width="755" height="220" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b9/Seal_of_Vatican_City.svg/220px-Seal_of_Vatican_City.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b9/Seal_of_Vatican_City.svg/330px-Seal_of_Vatican_City.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b9/Seal_of_Vatican_City.svg/440px-Seal_of_Vatican_City.svg.png 2x" width="220"/>
       </a>
       <div class="thumbcaption">
        <div class="magnify">
         <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Seal_of_Vatican_City.svg" title="Enlarge">
         </a>
        </div>
        The Seal of Vatican City. Note the use of the Italian language.
       </div>
      </div>
     </div>
     <p>
      Almost all of Vatican City's 558 (2005) citizens either live inside the Vatican's walls or serve in the Holy See's
      <a href="/wiki/List_of_diplomatic_missions_of_the_Holy_See" title="List of diplomatic missions of the Holy See">
       diplomatic service
      </a>
      in embassies (called "
      <a href="/wiki/Apostolic_Nunciature" title="Apostolic Nunciature">
       nunciatures
      </a>
      "; a papal ambassador is a "nuncio") around the world. The Vatican citizenry consists almost entirely of two groups: clergy, most of whom work in the service of the Holy See, and a very few as officials of the state; and the Swiss Guard. Most of the 2,400 lay workers who comprise the majority of the Vatican workforce reside outside the Vatican and are citizens of Italy, while a few are citizens of other nations. As a result, all of the City's actual citizens are Catholic as are all the
      <a href="/wiki/Place_of_worship" title="Place of worship">
       places of worship
      </a>
      .
     </p>
     <p>
      Vatican City has no formally enacted
      <a href="/wiki/Official_language" title="Official language">
       official language
      </a>
      , but, unlike the Holy See which most often uses
      <a href="/wiki/Latin" title="Latin">
       Latin
      </a>
      for the authoritative version of its official documents, Vatican City uses only Italian in its legislation and official communications.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-77">
       <a href="#cite_note-77">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        71
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      Italian is also the everyday language used by most of those who work in the state. In the
      <a href="/wiki/Swiss_Guard" title="Swiss Guard">
       Swiss Guard
      </a>
      , German is the language used for giving commands, but the individual guards take their oath of loyalty in their own languages: German, French,
      <a href="/wiki/Romansh_language" title="Romansh language">
       Romansh
      </a>
      or Italian. Vatican City's official website languages are Italian, English, French, German, and Spanish. (This site should not be confused with that of the Holy See, which uses all these languages, along with Portuguese, with Latin since 9 May 2008 and Chinese since 18 March 2009.)
     </p>
     <h3>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="Citizenship">
       Citizenship
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=Vatican_City&amp;action=edit&amp;section=21" title="Edit section: Citizenship">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h3>
     <p>
      Unlike
      <a href="/wiki/Citizenship" title="Citizenship">
       citizenship
      </a>
      of other states, which is based either on
      <i>
       <a href="/wiki/Jus_sanguinis" title="Jus sanguinis">
        jus sanguinis
       </a>
      </i>
      (birth from a citizen, even outside the state's territory) or on
      <i>
       <a href="/wiki/Jus_soli" title="Jus soli">
        jus soli
       </a>
      </i>
      (birth within the territory of the state), citizenship of Vatican City is granted
      <i>
       jus officii
      </i>
      , namely on the grounds of appointment to work in a certain capacity in the service of the Holy See. It usually ceases upon cessation of the appointment. Citizenship is extended also to the spouse, parents and descendants of a citizen, provided they are living with the person who is a citizen.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-78">
       <a href="#cite_note-78">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        72
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-79">
       <a href="#cite_note-79">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        73
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      The
      <a href="/wiki/Holy_See" title="Holy See">
       Holy See
      </a>
      , not being a country, issues only diplomatic and service passports, whereas Vatican City State issues normal passports for its citizens.
     </p>
     <p>
      Anyone who loses Vatican citizenship and does not possess other citizenship automatically becomes an
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Italian_citizenship" title="Italian citizenship">
       Italian citizen
      </a>
      as provided in the Lateran Treaty.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-treaty_39-2">
       <a href="#cite_note-treaty-39">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        34
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      As of 31 December 2005, there were, apart from the Pope himself, 557 people with Vatican citizenship, while there were 246 residents in the state who did not have its citizenship.
     </p>
     <p>
      Of the 557 citizens, 74% were clergy:
     </p>
     <ul>
      <li>
       58
       <a href="/wiki/Cardinal_(Catholicism)" title="Cardinal (Catholicism)">
        cardinals
       </a>
       , resident in Rome, mostly outside the Vatican;
      </li>
      <li>
       293 clergy, members of the Holy See's diplomatic missions, resident in other countries, and forming well over half the total of the citizens;
      </li>
      <li>
       62 other clergy, working but not necessarily living in the Vatican.
      </li>
     </ul>
     <p>
      The 101 members of the
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Pontifical_Swiss_Guard" title="Pontifical Swiss Guard">
       Pontifical Swiss Guard
      </a>
      constituted 18% of the total, and there were only 55 other lay persons with Vatican citizenship.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-80">
       <a href="#cite_note-80">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        74
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-LawNowAllows_81-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-LawNowAllows-81">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        75
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      On 22 February 2011, Pope Benedict XVI promulgated a new "Law concerning citizenship, residency and access" to Vatican City, which became effective on 1 March. It replaced the 1929 "Law concerning citizenship and residence".
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-82">
       <a href="#cite_note-82">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        76
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      There are 16 articles in the new law, whereas the old law had 33 articles.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-LawNowAllows_81-1">
       <a href="#cite_note-LawNowAllows-81">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        75
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      It updated the old law by incorporating changes made after 1929, such as the 1940 granting of Vatican City citizenship,
      <i>
       durante munere
      </i>
      , to the members of the Holy See's diplomatic service.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-83">
       <a href="#cite_note-83">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        77
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      It also created a new category, that of official Vatican "residents", i.e., people living in Vatican City; these are not necessarily Vatican citizens.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-LawNowAllows_81-2">
       <a href="#cite_note-LawNowAllows-81">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        75
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      On 1 March 2011, only 220 of the over 800 people living in Vatican City were citizens. There was a total of 572 Vatican citizens, of whom 352 were not residents, mainly
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Apostolic_nuncio" title="Apostolic nuncio">
       apostolic nuncios
      </a>
      and diplomatic staff.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-LawNowAllows_81-3">
       <a href="#cite_note-LawNowAllows-81">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        75
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <div class="thumb tnone" style="clear:both">
      <div class="thumbinner">
       <div class="overflowbugx" style="overflow: auto;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:View_from_Stpeters.jpg">
         <img alt="360-degree view from the dome of St. Peter's Basilica, looking over the Vatican's Saint Peter's Square (centre) and out into Rome, showing Vatican City in all directions." data-file-height="10620" data-file-width="50000" height="230" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f4/View_from_Stpeters.jpg/1083px-View_from_Stpeters.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f4/View_from_Stpeters.jpg/1625px-View_from_Stpeters.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f4/View_from_Stpeters.jpg/2166px-View_from_Stpeters.jpg 2x" width="1083"/>
        </a>
       </div>
       <div class="thumbcaption">
        <div class="magnify">
         <a href="/wiki/File:View_from_Stpeters.jpg" title="File:View from Stpeters.jpg">
         </a>
        </div>
        <center>
         360-degree view from the dome of
         <a href="/wiki/St._Peter%27s_Basilica" title="St. Peter's Basilica">
          St. Peter's Basilica
         </a>
         , looking over the Vatican's
         <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Saint_Peter%27s_Square" title="Saint Peter's Square">
          Saint Peter's Square
         </a>
         (centre) and out into Rome, showing Vatican City in all directions.
        </center>
       </div>
      </div>
     </div>
     <h2>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="Culture">
       Culture
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=Vatican_City&amp;action=edit&amp;section=22" title="Edit section: Culture">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h2>
     <div class="hatnote relarticle mainarticle">
      Main article:
      <a href="/wiki/Culture_of_Vatican_City" title="Culture of Vatican City">
       Culture of Vatican City
      </a>
     </div>
     <div class="hatnote">
      See also:
      <a href="/wiki/Music_of_Vatican_City" title="Music of Vatican City">
       Music of Vatican City
      </a>
     </div>
     <div class="thumb tright">
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
       <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:0_Chapelle_Sixtine_-_Palais_du_Belv%C3%A9d%C3%A8re_et_Mus%C3%A9es_du_Vatican.JPG">
        <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2592" data-file-width="3888" height="147" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/03/0_Chapelle_Sixtine_-_Palais_du_Belv%C3%A9d%C3%A8re_et_Mus%C3%A9es_du_Vatican.JPG/220px-0_Chapelle_Sixtine_-_Palais_du_Belv%C3%A9d%C3%A8re_et_Mus%C3%A9es_du_Vatican.JPG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/03/0_Chapelle_Sixtine_-_Palais_du_Belv%C3%A9d%C3%A8re_et_Mus%C3%A9es_du_Vatican.JPG/330px-0_Chapelle_Sixtine_-_Palais_du_Belv%C3%A9d%C3%A8re_et_Mus%C3%A9es_du_Vatican.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/03/0_Chapelle_Sixtine_-_Palais_du_Belv%C3%A9d%C3%A8re_et_Mus%C3%A9es_du_Vatican.JPG/440px-0_Chapelle_Sixtine_-_Palais_du_Belv%C3%A9d%C3%A8re_et_Mus%C3%A9es_du_Vatican.JPG 2x" width="220"/>
       </a>
       <div class="thumbcaption">
        <div class="magnify">
         <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:0_Chapelle_Sixtine_-_Palais_du_Belv%C3%A9d%C3%A8re_et_Mus%C3%A9es_du_Vatican.JPG" title="Enlarge">
         </a>
        </div>
        The
        <a href="/wiki/Vatican_Museums" title="Vatican Museums">
         Vatican Museums
        </a>
        (
        <i>
         Musei Vaticani
        </i>
        ) display works from the extensive collection of the Catholic Church
       </div>
      </div>
     </div>
     <p>
      Vatican City is home to some of the most famous art in the world.
      <a href="/wiki/St._Peter%27s_Basilica" title="St. Peter's Basilica">
       St. Peter's Basilica
      </a>
      , whose successive architects include
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Bramante" title="Bramante">
       Bramante
      </a>
      ,
      <a href="/wiki/Michelangelo" title="Michelangelo">
       Michelangelo
      </a>
      ,
      <a href="/wiki/Giacomo_della_Porta" title="Giacomo della Porta">
       Giacomo della Porta
      </a>
      ,
      <a href="/wiki/Carlo_Maderno" title="Carlo Maderno">
       Maderno
      </a>
      and
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Bernini" title="Bernini">
       Bernini
      </a>
      , is a renowned work of
      <a href="/wiki/Renaissance_architecture" title="Renaissance architecture">
       Renaissance architecture
      </a>
      . The
      <a href="/wiki/Sistine_Chapel" title="Sistine Chapel">
       Sistine Chapel
      </a>
      is famous for its frescos, which include works by
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Perugino" title="Perugino">
       Perugino
      </a>
      ,
      <a href="/wiki/Domenico_Ghirlandaio" title="Domenico Ghirlandaio">
       Domenico Ghirlandaio
      </a>
      and
      <a href="/wiki/Sandro_Botticelli" title="Sandro Botticelli">
       Botticelli
      </a>
      as well as the
      <a href="/wiki/Sistine_Chapel_ceiling" title="Sistine Chapel ceiling">
       ceiling
      </a>
      and
      <a href="/wiki/Last_Judgment" title="Last Judgment">
       Last Judgment
      </a>
      by
      <a href="/wiki/Michelangelo" title="Michelangelo">
       Michelangelo
      </a>
      . Artists who decorated the interiors of the Vatican include
      <a href="/wiki/Raphael" title="Raphael">
       Raphael
      </a>
      and
      <a href="/wiki/Fra_Angelico" title="Fra Angelico">
       Fra Angelico
      </a>
      .
     </p>
     <p>
      The
      <a href="/wiki/Vatican_Library" title="Vatican Library">
       Vatican Apostolic Library
      </a>
      and the collections of the
      <a href="/wiki/Vatican_Museums" title="Vatican Museums">
       Vatican Museums
      </a>
      are of the highest historical, scientific and cultural importance. In 1984, the Vatican was added by
      <a href="/wiki/UNESCO" title="UNESCO">
       UNESCO
      </a>
      to the List of
      <a href="/wiki/World_Heritage_Site" title="World Heritage Site">
       World Heritage Sites
      </a>
      ; it is the only one to consist of an entire state.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-UNESCO_84-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-UNESCO-84">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        78
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      Furthermore, it is the only site to date registered with the UNESCO as a
      <i>
       centre containing monuments
      </i>
      in the "International Register of Cultural Property under Special Protection" according to the 1954
      <a href="/wiki/Hague_Convention_for_the_Protection_of_Cultural_Property_in_the_Event_of_Armed_Conflict" title="Hague Convention for the Protection of Cultural Property in the Event of Armed Conflict">
       Hague Convention for the Protection of Cultural Property in the Event of Armed Conflict
      </a>
      .
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-UNESCO_84-1">
       <a href="#cite_note-UNESCO-84">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        78
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <table style="background:transparent;margin-top:0.5em">
      <tr>
       <td>

     <h2>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="Infrastructure">
       Infrastructure
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=Vatican_City&amp;action=edit&amp;section=23" title="Edit section: Infrastructure">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h2>
     <h3>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="Transport">
       Transport
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=Vatican_City&amp;action=edit&amp;section=24" title="Edit section: Transport">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h3>
     <div class="thumb tright">
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
       <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:0_Gare_du_Vatican.JPG">
        <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2528" data-file-width="3800" height="146" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/48/0_Gare_du_Vatican.JPG/220px-0_Gare_du_Vatican.JPG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/48/0_Gare_du_Vatican.JPG/330px-0_Gare_du_Vatican.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/48/0_Gare_du_Vatican.JPG/440px-0_Gare_du_Vatican.JPG 2x" width="220"/>
       </a>
       <div class="thumbcaption">
        <div class="magnify">
         <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:0_Gare_du_Vatican.JPG" title="Enlarge">
         </a>
        </div>
        <a href="/wiki/Rail_transport_in_Vatican_City" title="Rail transport in Vatican City">
         Vatican's Railway Station
        </a>
       </div>
      </div>
     </div>
     <div class="hatnote relarticle mainarticle">
      Main article:
      <a href="/wiki/Transport_in_Vatican_City" title="Transport in Vatican City">
       Transport in Vatican City
      </a>
     </div>
     <p>
      Vatican City has a reasonably well developed transport network considering its size (consisting mostly of a piazza and walkways). As a state that is 1.05kilometres (0.6mi) long and 0.85kilometres (0.5mi) wide,
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-86">
       <a href="#cite_note-86">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        80
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      it has a small
      <a href="/wiki/Transport_network" title="Transport network">
       transportation system
      </a>
      with no airports or highways. The only aviation facility in Vatican City is the
      <a href="/wiki/Vatican_City_Heliport" title="Vatican City Heliport">
       Vatican City Heliport
      </a>
      . There is a
      <a href="/wiki/Standard_gauge" title="Standard gauge">
       standard gauge
      </a>
      <a href="/wiki/Rail_transport_in_Vatican_City" title="Rail transport in Vatican City">
       railway
      </a>
      connected to Italy's network at Rome's Saint Peter's station by an 852-metre-long (932yd) spur, 300 metres (330yd) of which is within Vatican territory.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Sinfin_87-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-Sinfin-87">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        81
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      <a href="/wiki/Pope_John_XXIII" title="Pope John XXIII">
       Pope John XXIII
      </a>
      was the first Pope to make use of this railway.
      <a href="/wiki/Pope_John_Paul_II" title="Pope John Paul II">
       Pope John Paul II
      </a>
      rarely used it. The railway is mainly used to transport freight.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Sinfin_87-1">
       <a href="#cite_note-Sinfin-87">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        81
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      As Vatican City has no airports (it is one of the few
      <a href="/wiki/List_of_countries_without_an_airport" title="List of countries without an airport">
       independent states
      </a>
      in the world without one, except for the aforementioned heliport), it is served by the airports that serve the city of Rome, namely:
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Leonardo_da_Vinci-Fiumicino_Airport" title="Leonardo da Vinci-Fiumicino Airport">
       Leonardo da Vinci-Fiumicino Airport
      </a>
      and to a lesser extent,
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Rome_Ciampino_Airport" title="Rome Ciampino Airport">
       Ciampino Airport
      </a>
      , both of which serve as the departure gateway for the Pope's international visits.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Sinfin_87-2">
       <a href="#cite_note-Sinfin-87">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        81
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <h3>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="Communications">
       Communications
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=Vatican_City&amp;action=edit&amp;section=25" title="Edit section: Communications">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h3>
     <div class="thumb tright">
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;">
       <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Stamp_vending_machine_(Poste_Vaticane).jpg">
        <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2304" data-file-width="1728" height="227" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b1/Stamp_vending_machine_%28Poste_Vaticane%29.jpg/170px-Stamp_vending_machine_%28Poste_Vaticane%29.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b1/Stamp_vending_machine_%28Poste_Vaticane%29.jpg/255px-Stamp_vending_machine_%28Poste_Vaticane%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b1/Stamp_vending_machine_%28Poste_Vaticane%29.jpg/340px-Stamp_vending_machine_%28Poste_Vaticane%29.jpg 2x" width="170"/>
       </a>
       <div class="thumbcaption">
        <div class="magnify">
         <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Stamp_vending_machine_(Poste_Vaticane).jpg" title="Enlarge">
         </a>
        </div>
        The stamp vending machine of the Vatican Postal Service
       </div>
      </div>
     </div>
     <p>
      The City is served by an independent, modern telephone system,
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-88">
       <a href="#cite_note-88">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        82
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      the
      <a href="/wiki/Vatican_Pharmacy" title="Vatican Pharmacy">
       Vatican Pharmacy
      </a>
      , and post office. The
      <a href="/wiki/Mail" title="Mail">
       postal system
      </a>
      was founded on 11 February 1929, and two days later became operational. On 1 August, the state started to release its own postal stamps, under the authority of the
      <a href="/wiki/Philatelic_and_Numismatic_Office_of_the_Vatican_City_State" title="Philatelic and Numismatic Office of the Vatican City State">
       Philatelic and Numismatic Office of the Vatican City State
      </a>
      .
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-89">
       <a href="#cite_note-89">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        83
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      The City's
      <a href="/wiki/Mail" title="Mail">
       postal service
      </a>
      is sometimes recognised as "the best in the world"
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-NYT_90-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-NYT-90">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        84
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      and mail has been noted to arrive at its destination before the postal service in Rome.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-NYT_90-1">
       <a href="#cite_note-NYT-90">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        84
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      Vatican City also has its own telephone service, the
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Vatican_telephone_service" title="Vatican telephone service">
       Vatican telephone service
      </a>
      .
     </p>
     <p>
      The Vatican also controls its own Internet
      <a href="/wiki/Top-level_domain" title="Top-level domain">
       TLD
      </a>
      , which is registered as (
      <a href="/wiki/.va" title=".va">
       .va
      </a>
      ). Broadband service is widely provided within Vatican City. Vatican City has also been given a radio
      <a href="/wiki/ITU_prefix" title="ITU prefix">
       ITU prefix
      </a>
      , HV, and this is sometimes used by
      <a href="/wiki/Amateur_radio" title="Amateur radio">
       amateur radio
      </a>
      operators.
     </p>
     <p>
      <a href="/wiki/Vatican_Radio" title="Vatican Radio">
       Vatican Radio
      </a>
      , which was organised by
      <a href="/wiki/Guglielmo_Marconi" title="Guglielmo Marconi">
       Guglielmo Marconi
      </a>
      , broadcasts on
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Shortwave" title="Shortwave">
       short-wave
      </a>
      ,
      <a href="/wiki/Medium_wave" title="Medium wave">
       medium-wave
      </a>
      and FM frequencies and on the Internet.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-91">
       <a href="#cite_note-91">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        85
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      Its main transmission antennae are located in Italian territory. Television services are provided through another entity, the
      <a href="/wiki/Vatican_Television_Center" title="Vatican Television Center">
       Vatican Television Center
      </a>
      .
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-92">
       <a href="#cite_note-92">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        86
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      <i>
       <a href="/wiki/L%27Osservatore_Romano" title="L'Osservatore Romano">
        L'Osservatore Romano
       </a>
      </i>
      is the multilingual semi-official newspaper of the Holy See. It is published by a private corporation under the direction of Roman Catholic laymen, but reports on official information. However, the official texts of documents are in the
      <i>
       <a href="/wiki/Acta_Apostolicae_Sedis" title="Acta Apostolicae Sedis">
        Acta Apostolicae Sedis
       </a>
      </i>
      , the
      <a href="/wiki/Gazette" title="Gazette">
       official gazette
      </a>
      of the Holy See, which has an appendix for documents of the Vatican City State.
     </p>
     <p>
      Vatican Radio, the Vatican Television Center, and L'Osservatore Romano are organs not of the Vatican State but of the Holy See, and are listed as such in the
      <a href="/wiki/Annuario_Pontificio" title="Annuario Pontificio">
       Annuario Pontificio
      </a>
      , which places them in the section "Institutions linked with the Holy See", ahead of the sections on the Holy See's diplomatic service abroad and the
      <a href="/wiki/Diplomatic_corps" title="Diplomatic corps">
       Diplomatic corps
      </a>
      accredited to the Holy See, after which is placed the section on the State of Vatican City.
     </p>
     <h2>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="Crime">
       Crime
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=Vatican_City&amp;action=edit&amp;section=26" title="Edit section: Crime">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h2>
     <div class="hatnote relarticle mainarticle">
      Main article:
      <a href="/wiki/Crime_in_Vatican_City" title="Crime in Vatican City">
       Crime in Vatican City
      </a>
     </div>
     <p>
      Crime in Vatican City consists largely of purse snatching,
      <a href="/wiki/Pickpocketing" title="Pickpocketing">
       pickpocketing
      </a>
      and shoplifting by outsiders.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-crime_rate_93-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-crime_rate-93">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        87
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      The tourist foot-traffic in
      <a href="/wiki/St._Peter%27s_Square" title="St. Peter's Square">
       St. Peter's Square
      </a>
      is one of the main locations for pickpockets in Vatican City.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-94">
       <a href="#cite_note-94">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        88
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      If crimes are committed in Saint Peter's Square, the perpetrators may be arrested and tried by the Italian authorities, since that area is normally patrolled by Italian police.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-95">
       <a href="#cite_note-95">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        89
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      Under the terms of article 22 the Lateran Treaty,
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-treaty1_96-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-treaty1-96">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        90
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      Italy will, at the request of the Holy See, punish individuals for crimes committed within Vatican City and will itself proceed against the person who committed the offence, if that person takes refuge in Italian territory. Persons accused of crimes recognized as such both in Italy and in Vatican City that are committed in Italian territory will be handed over to the Italian authorities if they take refuge in Vatican City or in buildings that under the treaty enjoy immunity.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-treaty1_96-1">
       <a href="#cite_note-treaty1-96">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        90
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-97">
       <a href="#cite_note-97">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        91
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      Vatican City has no prison system, apart from a few detention cells for pre-trial detention.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-98">
       <a href="#cite_note-98">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        92
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      People convicted of committing crimes in the Vatican serve terms in
      <a href="/wiki/Italy" title="Italy">
       Italian
      </a>
      prisons (
      <a href="/wiki/Polizia_Penitenziaria" title="Polizia Penitenziaria">
       Polizia Penitenziaria
      </a>
      ), with costs covered by the Vatican.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-99">
       <a href="#cite_note-99">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        93
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>

     <h2>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="References">

      </span>

       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
